Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Steps to reproduce the problem:

<br>





1.the first step is similar as  



<span class="line"><!---->1.the first step is similar as  <!----></span>





issue 1244188



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1244188" title="uaf in content::MediaStreamDispatcherHost::OnWebContentsFocused"><!---->issue 1244188<!----></a>



<br>





2.1. Apply the attached token.patch (*)



<span class="line"><!---->2.1. Apply the attached token.patch (*)<!----></span>



<br>





2. $ python ./copy_mojo_js_bindings.py /path/to/chrome/.../out/asan/gen



<span class="line"><!---->2. $ python ./copy_mojo_js_bindings.py /path/to/chrome/.../out/asan/gen<!----></span>

   $ python -m SimpleHTTPServer



<span class="line"><!---->   $ python -m SimpleHTTPServer<!----></span>

3. Start chrome and visit poc.html with the "--enable-blink-features=MojoJS" (emulates a compromised renderer)



<span class="line"><!---->3. Start chrome and visit poc.html with the "--enable-blink-features=MojoJS" (emulates a compromised renderer)<!----></span>

3.when visit poc.html, you should choose the entire screen, and before it reset, you should click the button of "capture", and alt+f4 close the window quickly, I just cause the similar access_violation stack race as 



<span class="line"><!---->3.when visit poc.html, you should choose the entire screen, and before it reset, you should click the button of "capture", and alt+f4 close the window quickly, I just cause the similar access_violation stack race as <!----></span>





issue 1242036



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1242036" title="uaf in content::DesktopCaptureDevice::Core::AllocateAndStart"><!---->issue 1242036<!----></a>





,

The attached stack trace is a null pointer deref. I'm not familiar enough with the IPC systems involved to understand if triggering an actual use-after-free is something a renderer can directly trigger.



<span class="line"><!---->The attached stack trace is a null pointer deref. I'm not familiar enough with the IPC systems involved to understand if triggering an actual use-after-free is something a renderer can directly trigger.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





To avoid bifurcating the discussion too much, I'm going to dupe the (older, definitely use-after-free) 



<span class="line"><!---->To avoid bifurcating the discussion too much, I'm going to dupe the (older, definitely use-after-free) <!----></span>





issue 1242036



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1242036" title="uaf in content::DesktopCaptureDevice::Core::AllocateAndStart"><!---->issue 1242036<!----></a>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





into this one since we're still trying to understand if this is reachable via a renderer.



<span class="line"><!---->into this one since we're still trying to understand if this is reachable via a renderer.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





There is 100% a use-after-free bug in this code:



<span class="line"><!---->There is 100% a use-after-free bug in this code:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. We post a task to a helper thread here with a base::Unretained pointer to content::DesktopCaptureDevice::Core here: 



<span class="line"><!---->1. We post a task to a helper thread here with a base::Unretained pointer to content::DesktopCaptureDevice::Core here: <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:content/browser/media/capture/desktop_capture_device.cc;l=593;drc=97d6e9c16991a75919ef817a700df1884bf022e1



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:content/browser/media/capture/desktop_capture_device.cc;l=593;drc=97d6e9c16991a75919ef817a700df1884bf022e1"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:content/browser/media/capture/desktop_capture_device.cc;l=593;drc=97d6e9c16991a75919ef817a700df1884bf022e1<!----></a>



<br>





2. We attempt to always delete the Core object on `thread_`: 



<span class="line"><!---->2. We attempt to always delete the Core object on `thread_`: <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:content/browser/media/capture/desktop_capture_device.cc;l=598;drc=97d6e9c16991a75919ef817a700df1884bf022e1



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:content/browser/media/capture/desktop_capture_device.cc;l=598;drc=97d6e9c16991a75919ef817a700df1884bf022e1"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:content/browser/media/capture/desktop_capture_device.cc;l=598;drc=97d6e9c16991a75919ef817a700df1884bf022e1<!----></a>



<br>





3. However, we don't delete the Core object on `thread_` if `DesktopCaptureDevice` itself is destroyed and we haven't called `StopAndDeAllocate`.



<span class="line"><!---->3. However, we don't delete the Core object on `thread_` if `DesktopCaptureDevice` itself is destroyed and we haven't called `StopAndDeAllocate`.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I'm guessing that the desktop capture code has some internal invariants that are supposed to protect against deleting `DesktopCaptureDevice` without stopping it first—except there is one edge case where it can happen. Looking as the use-after-free stacks attached to 



<span class="line"><!---->I'm guessing that the desktop capture code has some internal invariants that are supposed to protect against deleting `DesktopCaptureDevice` without stopping it first—except there is one edge case where it can happen. Looking as the use-after-free stacks attached to <!----></span>





issue 1242036



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1242036" title="uaf in content::DesktopCaptureDevice::Core::AllocateAndStart"><!---->issue 1242036<!----></a>





, 



<span class="line"><!---->, <!----></span>





they happen because of this line from 



<span class="line"><!---->they happen because of this line from <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:content/browser/renderer_host/media/in_process_video_capture_device_launcher.cc;l=421;drc=5bc57681793ef5008225cf26900492f62f640dd0



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:content/browser/renderer_host/media/in_process_video_capture_device_launcher.cc;l=421;drc=5bc57681793ef5008225cf26900492f62f640dd0"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:content/browser/renderer_host/media/in_process_video_capture_device_launcher.cc;l=421;drc=5bc57681793ef5008225cf26900492f62f640dd0<!----></a>





:



<span class="line"><!---->:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  std::move(result_callback).Run(std::move(video_capture_device));



<span class="line"><!---->  std::move(result_callback).Run(std::move(video_capture_device));<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The problem is that `result_callback` is a callback created by `base::BindPostTask()`. Internally, BindPostTask binds the arguments passed to `Run()` to a new callback and attempts to `PostTask()` the new callback to the correct sequence. However, if the `PostTask()` fails... we delete the newly-created callback (which we passed ownership of `video_capture_device` to by virtue of binding it!). This deletes `video_capture_device`, and now `content::DesktopCaptureDevice::Core` has been racily destroyed on the wrong thread. Oops.



<span class="line"><!---->The problem is that `result_callback` is a callback created by `base::BindPostTask()`. Internally, BindPostTask binds the arguments passed to `Run()` to a new callback and attempts to `PostTask()` the new callback to the correct sequence. However, if the `PostTask()` fails... we delete the newly-created callback (which we passed ownership of `video_capture_device` to by virtue of binding it!). This deletes `video_capture_device`, and now `content::DesktopCaptureDevice::Core` has been racily destroyed on the wrong thread. Oops.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





joedow@, I'm assigning to you to help us understand if this is something a compromised renderer could trigger *without* requiring user interaction. I'm not familiar enough with how the desktop capture flow is started/stopped to definitively say.



<span class="line"><!---->joedow@, I'm assigning to you to help us understand if this is something a compromised renderer could trigger *without* requiring user interaction. I'm not familiar enough with how the desktop capture flow is started/stopped to definitively say.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I'm not sure where the right fix is at this point. We've had issues in the past with PostTask() failing, and I don't think we definitively have a right way of handling these sort of bugs / preventing them :( CCing danakj/gab/kylechar for thoughts...



<span class="line"><!---->I'm not sure where the right fix is at this point. We've had issues in the past with PostTask() failing, and I don't think we definitively have a right way of handling these sort of bugs / preventing them :( CCing danakj/gab/kylechar for thoughts...<!----></span>

<strong><!---->Components:</strong>


          


          

-Internals>Media>SurfaceCapture Internals>Media>ScreenCapture


          




          

<br>


        




        




      

<div class="issue-diff">
        <!---->
          <strong><!---->Components:</strong>
          
          -Internals&gt;Media&gt;SurfaceCapture Internals&gt;Media&gt;ScreenCapture
          
          <br>
        <!---->
        
      </div>

<br>


    


        


      


        









The desktop capturer should not be able to be started without some kind of user gesture and consent flow (whether through a permissions dialog, or through the system UI in the case of ChromeOS).  Those are required before the renderer can get an unguessable token to pass with the IPC to start capture.



<span class="line"><!---->The desktop capturer should not be able to be started without some kind of user gesture and consent flow (whether through a permissions dialog, or through the system UI in the case of ChromeOS).  Those are required before the renderer can get an unguessable token to pass with the IPC to start capture.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It looks like the PoC is passing a dummy token, but still requires the user to go through the screen share permissions dialog.



<span class="line"><!---->It looks like the PoC is passing a dummy token, but still requires the user to go through the screen share permissions dialog.<!----></span>

Starting to look into this now that I'm back; dcheng/kylechar/gab/danakj, were there any thoughts you all had about the post task failing? It seems like that destruction path is what's triggering this UAF?



<span class="line"><!---->Starting to look into this now that I'm back; dcheng/kylechar/gab/danakj, were there any thoughts you all had about the post task failing? It seems like that destruction path is what's triggering this UAF?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I'm going to guess that despite the comment that the Stop/Join call should be quick, that we can't simply try to call StopAndDeAllocate in the CaptureDevice destructor if it still has a core_ object? 



<span class="line"><!---->I'm going to guess that despite the comment that the Stop/Join call should be quick, that we can't simply try to call StopAndDeAllocate in the CaptureDevice destructor if it still has a core_ object? <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





However, I'd also guess that if the PostTask there failed, we likely wouldn't be in a good state to try to post an additional task/stop the thread....



<span class="line"><!---->However, I'd also guess that if the PostTask there failed, we likely wouldn't be in a good state to try to post an additional task/stop the thread....<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The core object already seems to have a weak pointer factory, I believe it's safe to create one of those on any thread as long as they are only checked on a single thread (the one the task is posted to?); but I'm unsure if there's any weirdness with that invalidation if it is destroyed on the wrong thread...



<span class="line"><!---->The core object already seems to have a weak pointer factory, I believe it's safe to create one of those on any thread as long as they are only checked on a single thread (the one the task is posted to?); but I'm unsure if there's any weirdness with that invalidation if it is destroyed on the wrong thread...<!----></span>

> Starting to look into this now that I'm back; dcheng/kylechar/gab/danakj, were there any thoughts you all had about the post task failing? It seems like that destruction path is what's triggering this UAF?



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; Starting to look into this now that I'm back; dcheng/kylechar/gab/danakj, were there any thoughts you all had about the post task failing? It seems like that destruction path is what's triggering this UAF?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In general binding an object that has invariants about when/where it must be destroyed in a callback and posting that callback to another thread is problematic. If a PostTask() fails the callback (and any bound objects) will be immediately destroyed, possibly at an unexpected time or on the wrong thread. The callback being run at [1] binds |video_capture_device| into a OnceClosure and then PostTasks it.



<span class="line"><!---->In general binding an object that has invariants about when/where it must be destroyed in a callback and posting that callback to another thread is problematic. If a PostTask() fails the callback (and any bound objects) will be immediately destroyed, possibly at an unexpected time or on the wrong thread. The callback being run at [1] binds |video_capture_device| into a OnceClosure and then PostTasks it.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So it looks like:



<span class="line"><!---->So it looks like:<!----></span>



<br>





1.  InProcessVideoCaptureDeviceLauncher::LaunchDeviceAsync() runs on one thread. It creates |after_start_capture_callback| which will PostTask back to the current thread [2]. A task is posted to run DoStartDesktopCaptureOnDeviceThread() on another thread [3] which includes |after_start_capture_callback| as |result_callback|.



<span class="line"><!---->1.  InProcessVideoCaptureDeviceLauncher::LaunchDeviceAsync() runs on one thread. It creates |after_start_capture_callback| which will PostTask back to the current thread [2]. A task is posted to run DoStartDesktopCaptureOnDeviceThread() on another thread [3] which includes |after_start_capture_callback| as |result_callback|.<!----></span>



<br>





2. InProcessVideoCaptureDeviceLauncher::DoStartDesktopCaptureOnDeviceThread() runs on the other thread. |result_callback| is run with |video_capture_device|. This tries to PostTask back to the original thread.



<span class="line"><!---->2. InProcessVideoCaptureDeviceLauncher::DoStartDesktopCaptureOnDeviceThread() runs on the other thread. |result_callback| is run with |video_capture_device|. This tries to PostTask back to the original thread.<!----></span>



<br>





3. The PostTask fails and |video_capture_device| is destroyed in the wrong place.



<span class="line"><!---->3. The PostTask fails and |video_capture_device| is destroyed in the wrong place.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I don't know enough about media stack to understand why the post task fails.



<span class="line"><!---->I don't know enough about media stack to understand why the post task fails.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->&gt; It's worth noting that the token patch requested is also applied to the browser process. <!----></span>

<div>

        by

<div role="heading" class="comment-header" aria-level="2">
        <div>
          <a class="comment-link" href="?id=1244205#c31">Comment 31<!----></a>

          
        by
        <mr-user-link></mr-user-link>
        on
        <chops-timestamp title="Mon, Jan 10, 2022, 2:54 PM EST"></chops-timestamp>

I understand this code a little bit better now. DesktopCaptureDevice spins up a new thread, which it holds. It then has a child object, core, which lives on that thread. Calls to DesktopCaptureDevice post tasks to that thread, with a base::Unretained (presuming this is safe under the assumption that we control the lifetime). Interestingly the core child object *does* have a Weak Pointer Factory, but it is currently unused. 



<span class="line"><!---->I understand this code a little bit better now. DesktopCaptureDevice spins up a new thread, which it holds. It then has a child object, core, which lives on that thread. Calls to DesktopCaptureDevice post tasks to that thread, with a base::Unretained (presuming this is safe under the assumption that we control the lifetime). Interestingly the core child object *does* have a Weak Pointer Factory, but it is currently unused. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Looking at the class declaration, it looks like the core object is declared after the thread object, which means that when we go to destroy the object, the Core object gets destroyed and *then* the thread object (which should be calling stop in it's destructor IIUC), is destroyed. However, with base::Unretained, this could cause a race wherein the thread hasn't been destroyed but the core object has, which I suspect could cause this issue.



<span class="line"><!---->Looking at the class declaration, it looks like the core object is declared after the thread object, which means that when we go to destroy the object, the Core object gets destroyed and *then* the thread object (which should be calling stop in it's destructor IIUC), is destroyed. However, with base::Unretained, this could cause a race wherein the thread hasn't been destroyed but the core object has, which I suspect could cause this issue.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





There's a DCHECK in the destructor that StopAndDeAllocate was called, which a situation like this probably wouldn't fix. We've got a couple of options here, none of which are mutually exclusive:



<span class="line"><!---->There's a DCHECK in the destructor that StopAndDeAllocate was called, which a situation like this probably wouldn't fix. We've got a couple of options here, none of which are mutually exclusive:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1) Switch base::Unretained to use the WeakPtr for the Core object, WeakPtr's aren't used on Any other thread, so creating them for the sole purpose of binding to a single task runner should be safe.



<span class="line"><!---->1) Switch base::Unretained to use the WeakPtr for the Core object, WeakPtr's aren't used on Any other thread, so creating them for the sole purpose of binding to a single task runner should be safe.<!----></span>



<br>





2) Switch the declared order of Core/Thread, so that the Thread is the first DesktopCaptureDevice member destroyed



<span class="line"><!---->2) Switch the declared order of Core/Thread, so that the Thread is the first DesktopCaptureDevice member destroyed<!----></span>



<br>





3) Call StopAndDeAllocate in the Destructor.



<span class="line"><!---->3) Call StopAndDeAllocate in the Destructor.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I'm disinclined to do #3, as I think that may hide a pattern where a legitimate consumer is holding it wrong; though the DCHECK makes it not apply to production builds, and likely a CHECK could trigger an edge case like this one, where the object hasn't *actually* been started, but the start is pending/queued.



<span class="line"><!---->I'm disinclined to do #3, as I think that may hide a pattern where a legitimate consumer is holding it wrong; though the DCHECK makes it not apply to production builds, and likely a CHECK could trigger an edge case like this one, where the object hasn't *actually* been started, but the start is pending/queued.<!----></span>

Mark brought that up as well, and proposed keeping the destruction order as-is, but with Core being created with a base::OnTaskRunnerDeleter; but I'm inclined to agree that this should be a non-issue, as if it's thread is deleted on the same thread (via joining during Stop), then that effectively becomes the new "safe" thread for deleting the object.



<span class="line"><!---->Mark brought that up as well, and proposed keeping the destruction order as-is, but with Core being created with a base::OnTaskRunnerDeleter; but I'm inclined to agree that this should be a non-issue, as if it's thread is deleted on the same thread (via joining during Stop), then that effectively becomes the new "safe" thread for deleting the object.<!----></span>

<br>

Sorry, missed kyle's part about the DCHECK; technically the DCHECK(!core_) in the destructor would fail first; and since it's a DCHECK it shouldn't be triggered on a production build; but on a developer/debug build this is a signal that a dev is almost certainly holding it wrong (as I've been unable to make this issue repro otherwise).



<span class="line"><!---->Sorry, missed kyle's part about the DCHECK; technically the DCHECK(!core_) in the destructor would fail first; and since it's a DCHECK it shouldn't be triggered on a production build; but on a developer/debug build this is a signal that a dev is almost certainly holding it wrong (as I've been unable to make this issue repro otherwise).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





After talking with Mark, I don't think he's opposed (and indeed we may want to look at changing the device contract if we can), to calling StopAndDeAllocate in the destructor, if we feel that's better than keeping the dcheck.



<span class="line"><!---->After talking with Mark, I don't think he's opposed (and indeed we may want to look at changing the device contract if we can), to calling StopAndDeAllocate in the destructor, if we feel that's better than keeping the dcheck.<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

Convert issue to new template structure
